# AI Pricing and ROI: A Technical Breakdown

> There has been an immense interest in generative AI recently, but many organizations struggle to understand and forecast cost and revenue opportunities. If you’re creating or approving AI budgets, you’ll want to know the details. In this course, Denys Linkov breaks down the cost factors of operating AI models in a business environment. He addresses key questions like how to weigh a build versus bu

### 1. Build vs. Buy

#### Framing build vs. buy in an AI context
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/framing-build-vs-buy-in-an-ai-context?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/framing-build-vs-buy-in-an-ai-context?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] AI is a powerful technology to incorporate into your business.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/framing-build-vs-buy-in-an-ai-context?u=76281980&t=4)** But how should you get started?
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/framing-build-vs-buy-in-an-ai-context?u=76281980&t=6)** In this video, we'll cover how to start exploring the build versus buy journey of AI.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/framing-build-vs-buy-in-an-ai-context?u=76281980&t=11)** Now, if we were having this discussion five years ago, build versus buy would generally mean run in-house versus outsource.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/framing-build-vs-buy-in-an-ai-context?u=76281980&t=20)** But now, with the advances of gen AI and offered solutions, many more solutions work out of the box and off the shelf.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/framing-build-vs-buy-in-an-ai-context?u=76281980&t=27)** AI can solve a number of problems and will depend on the industry.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/framing-build-vs-buy-in-an-ai-context?u=76281980&t=31)** A hospital may benefit from better patient summaries and transcriptions.
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/framing-build-vs-buy-in-an-ai-context?u=76281980&t=36)** An E-commerce store can grow faster with better photo editing.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/framing-build-vs-buy-in-an-ai-context?u=76281980&t=40)** Or a car manufacturer could do better predictive maintenance.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/framing-build-vs-buy-in-an-ai-context?u=76281980&t=44)** It's important to understand the scope of your initial AI projects and the capabilities of your existing organization.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/framing-build-vs-buy-in-an-ai-context?u=76281980&t=50)** Building in-house is most efficient when you have the talent and software infrastructure to support such a project.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/framing-build-vs-buy-in-an-ai-context?u=76281980&t=57)** Thankfully, over the past five years, cloud providers and open source libraries have made it significantly easier to train, deploy, and manage models.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/framing-build-vs-buy-in-an-ai-context?u=76281980&t=67)** Similar gains have been recognized by many vendors, with managed services now simpler than ever to use, some just being an API call away.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/framing-build-vs-buy-in-an-ai-context?u=76281980&t=76)** Industry-specific solutions often come with vendor expertise, allowing you to leverage these teams to implement your specific solutions.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/framing-build-vs-buy-in-an-ai-context?u=76281980&t=85)** If you're in a regulated industry, such as financial services or healthcare, more attention should be placed on privacy, user disclosure, and regulatory compliance.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/framing-build-vs-buy-in-an-ai-context?u=76281980&t=96)** You may also have proprietary and sensitive data that must be kept in-house.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/framing-build-vs-buy-in-an-ai-context?u=76281980&t=101)** So deciding build versus buy isn't so different from any other decision.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/framing-build-vs-buy-in-an-ai-context?u=76281980&t=106)** So let's take a look into the landscape in our next set of videos.

#### Setup vs. ongoing costs
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/setup-vs-ongoing-costs?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/setup-vs-ongoing-costs?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] AI systems don't just take time to develop.
>
> **[0:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/setup-vs-ongoing-costs?u=76281980&t=3)** They need to be actively maintained and monitored.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/setup-vs-ongoing-costs?u=76281980&t=6)** Let's break down what the setup and ongoing costs of an AI solution looks like.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/setup-vs-ongoing-costs?u=76281980&t=11)** In the AI world.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/setup-vs-ongoing-costs?u=76281980&t=12)** We typically divide model development into two phases, model training and deployment.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/setup-vs-ongoing-costs?u=76281980&t=18)** Model training involves researching the problem, gathering the appropriate data, selecting the right model type, and training it.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/setup-vs-ongoing-costs?u=76281980&t=27)** This journey is typically challenging as it exposes some organizational weaknesses, like which concrete business problems AI can solve, or messy data.
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/setup-vs-ongoing-costs?u=76281980&t=36)** These problems can be solved, but are usually ignored in the initial assessment.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/setup-vs-ongoing-costs?u=76281980&t=41)** Model training usually requires a significant amount of R&D from a business standpoint, and also a technological one.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/setup-vs-ongoing-costs?u=76281980&t=48)** From a finance perspective, we can classify this as a capital expense.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/setup-vs-ongoing-costs?u=76281980&t=53)** Rather than training your own model, you can also purchase or license models.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/setup-vs-ongoing-costs?u=76281980&t=58)** After a model is trained, it needs to be deployed, and integrated with existing systems.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/setup-vs-ongoing-costs?u=76281980&t=63)** This might also require significant innovation depending on your business problem.
>
> **[1:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/setup-vs-ongoing-costs?u=76281980&t=68)** Privacy, latency, throughput, and network connectivity would all affect the deployment pattern that you choose in the product configurations you would have.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/setup-vs-ongoing-costs?u=76281980&t=78)** Once the models and their infrastructure are up and running, they're typically classified as an operating expense or OpEx.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/setup-vs-ongoing-costs?u=76281980&t=86)** In most modern applications, you'll need to continuously monitor and update your models, which is typically referred to as MLOps.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/setup-vs-ongoing-costs?u=76281980&t=94)** Like software, models aren't static, and need to be updated and retrained.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/setup-vs-ongoing-costs?u=76281980&t=99)** So these are the key considerations for model setup and ongoing expenses.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/setup-vs-ongoing-costs?u=76281980&t=104)** In the next video, we'll discuss selecting the right model for the task.

#### Selecting the right models for the tasks
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/selecting-the-right-models-for-the-tasks?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/selecting-the-right-models-for-the-tasks?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] These days, everyone wants to use GenAI, but is it the right tool for the job?
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/selecting-the-right-models-for-the-tasks?u=76281980&t=6)** GenAI typically uses large and compute-intensive models, so the best way to save money is not to run them, so it's important to choose the right model for the right use case.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/selecting-the-right-models-for-the-tasks?u=76281980&t=16)** Let's go through some examples.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/selecting-the-right-models-for-the-tasks?u=76281980&t=18)** Tabular data, which usually involves predicting numeric properties, like the size of a loan, is typically best done with boosting or tree-based methods.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/selecting-the-right-models-for-the-tasks?u=76281980&t=28)** Forecasting models such as predicting time series results like the sales of the next month, typically use moving average models and deep learning.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/selecting-the-right-models-for-the-tasks?u=76281980&t=37)** Recommender systems serve up the recommendations that we see on social media or e-commerce sites.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/selecting-the-right-models-for-the-tasks?u=76281980&t=43)** Typically, there's been a lot of success there with deep learning.
>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/selecting-the-right-models-for-the-tasks?u=76281980&t=47)** Well-defined language tasks like sentiment analysis or translation are also done very well without GenAI.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/selecting-the-right-models-for-the-tasks?u=76281980&t=54)** Now, GenAI models can be great at tasks like summarization, data extraction, image generation, and many more.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/selecting-the-right-models-for-the-tasks?u=76281980&t=62)** Their best use case, however, is to adapt and prototype to new tasks, allowing you to experiment and understand the intended goal without spending time gathering the data and infrastructure to deploy to specialized model.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/selecting-the-right-models-for-the-tasks?u=76281980&t=75)** The next video, we'll cover the best ways to deploy your models using the choice of SaaS, Paas, and IaaS solutions in the AI context.

#### SaaS, PaaS, and IaaS in the context of AI
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/saas-paas-and-iaas-in-the-context-of-ai?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/saas-paas-and-iaas-in-the-context-of-ai?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Most IT organizations categorize their infrastructure spend.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/saas-paas-and-iaas-in-the-context-of-ai?u=76281980&t=4)** So how can we do the same thing with AI infrastructure?
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/saas-paas-and-iaas-in-the-context-of-ai?u=76281980&t=8)** When we talk about cloud infrastructure, we typically divide them into categories to understand their capabilities in how to make buying decisions.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/saas-paas-and-iaas-in-the-context-of-ai?u=76281980&t=16)** These are often referred to as SaaS, PaaS, and IaaS.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/saas-paas-and-iaas-in-the-context-of-ai?u=76281980&t=20)** As a quick refresher, IaaS stands for infrastructure as a service, PaaS stands for platform as a service, SaaS stands for software as a service, and in the AI world, MaaS stands for model as a service.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/saas-paas-and-iaas-in-the-context-of-ai?u=76281980&t=33)** Let's go through some examples with a situation where we want to train a model.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/saas-paas-and-iaas-in-the-context-of-ai?u=76281980&t=38)** IaaS typically refers to as a basic set of compute, and in the AI context, this might be VMs with GPU support.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/saas-paas-and-iaas-in-the-context-of-ai?u=76281980&t=46)** These would be useful if your company is building something very bespoke and needs more control.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/saas-paas-and-iaas-in-the-context-of-ai?u=76281980&t=51)** PaaS in the AI context would be a platform custom tailored for training models and providing an opinionated way to do so.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/saas-paas-and-iaas-in-the-context-of-ai?u=76281980&t=58)** This might be a framework like Kubeflow.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/saas-paas-and-iaas-in-the-context-of-ai?u=76281980&t=61)** SaaS in an AI context usually involves an opinionated offering where you can do the task end-to-end with minimal configuration.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/saas-paas-and-iaas-in-the-context-of-ai?u=76281980&t=70)** This might be like the OpenAI fine-tuning API.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/saas-paas-and-iaas-in-the-context-of-ai?u=76281980&t=73)** Now MaaS, model as a service, is as simple as calling an API and getting a response.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/saas-paas-and-iaas-in-the-context-of-ai?u=76281980&t=79)** This might be like calling Claude, a model from Anthropic, where you give it some input and receive an output.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/saas-paas-and-iaas-in-the-context-of-ai?u=76281980&t=85)** And between the cloud space and the AI space, things do get a little bit different.
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/saas-paas-and-iaas-in-the-context-of-ai?u=76281980&t=90)** Definitions can typically blend, especially in the PaaS and SaaS spectrum.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/saas-paas-and-iaas-in-the-context-of-ai?u=76281980&t=96)** Let's take for example, Hugging Face.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/saas-paas-and-iaas-in-the-context-of-ai?u=76281980&t=99)** Is Hugging Face a PaaS or a SaaS?
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/saas-paas-and-iaas-in-the-context-of-ai?u=76281980&t=101)** On one hand, it's a PaaS because it uses its open-source libraries to provide an opinionated way to build and serve AI models.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/saas-paas-and-iaas-in-the-context-of-ai?u=76281980&t=109)** On the other hand, there's a simple managed solution that Hugging Face provides for serving these models.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/saas-paas-and-iaas-in-the-context-of-ai?u=76281980&t=115)** Now, another example is a different set of PaaS complexities between different platforms.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/saas-paas-and-iaas-in-the-context-of-ai?u=76281980&t=120)** Some platforms like Hugging Face have few features, and are simple to use.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/saas-paas-and-iaas-in-the-context-of-ai?u=76281980&t=125)** On the other hand, there are more comprehensive offerings like SageMaker, which has many features that you can configure.
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/saas-paas-and-iaas-in-the-context-of-ai?u=76281980&t=131)** And it's very easy to get caught up in the minutiae of what is a PaaS or what is a SaaS in the AI context.
>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/saas-paas-and-iaas-in-the-context-of-ai?u=76281980&t=137)** The important thing here is to focus on the key decision points when deciding what kind of solution you'll implement.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/saas-paas-and-iaas-in-the-context-of-ai?u=76281980&t=144)** Here are six important decision points to use.
>
> **[2:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/saas-paas-and-iaas-in-the-context-of-ai?u=76281980&t=146)** These are the time to market, integration points, available data, team structure, domain area, and compliance requirements.
>
> **[2:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/saas-paas-and-iaas-in-the-context-of-ai?u=76281980&t=156)** These will be important and something that we'll reference when making a decision on implementing an AI platform.
>
> **[2:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/saas-paas-and-iaas-in-the-context-of-ai?u=76281980&t=162)** In the next video, we'll talk about the costs of using an AI API, the simplest way to integrate with AI.

### 2. Costs of Using an AI API

#### Introduction to AI as an API
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-an-api?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-an-api?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] The magical experience of Gen AI via an API is that if you can dream an idea, you can usually prototype it.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-an-api?u=76281980&t=7)** This is a stark comparison with many more traditional ML tools, which require exploration, tuning, and adjustment.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-an-api?u=76281980&t=14)** Let's go through some questions to ask when assessing an AI as an API.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-an-api?u=76281980&t=19)** These factors include our existing ones, time to market, integration points, available data, team structure, domain areas, and compliance requirements.

>

>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-an-api?u=76281980&t=44)** The biggest advantage for AI as an API is time to market.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-an-api?u=76281980&t=48)** The faster you can launch your product to market, the bigger your advantage.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-an-api?u=76281980&t=51)** An early example is language translation as a way to easily integrate AI into your application.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-an-api?u=76281980&t=58)** Since then, we have applications like traffic prediction, image classification, and many more.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-an-api?u=76281980&t=64)** This allows us to validate our ideas quickly and figure out which type of AI we actually need.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-an-api?u=76281980&t=70)** Moving on to our second factor, which is reliability.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-an-api?u=76281980&t=74)** In the early days of OpenAI, the ChatGPT API often failed.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-an-api?u=76281980&t=79)** This made depending on the API a challenge.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-an-api?u=76281980&t=81)** Since then, the OpenAI APIs have gotten a lot more reliable, and you can check the reliability on their website at status.[openai.com](https://openai.com).
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-an-api?u=76281980&t=91)** Now what makes reliability complex is that the model not only has to offer uptime, but also has to offer the correct answer and have the usual latencies that we expect.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-an-api?u=76281980&t=101)** If the AI API is very core to your business, it might be important to consider a multi AI strategy where you might use multiple AI providers to make sure that your service is at least working.
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-an-api?u=76281980&t=112)** In the ChatGPT case, OpenAI has a program called the Foundry program where you can pay extra to have additional capacity that's pre reserved.
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-an-api?u=76281980&t=121)** Now API costs can quickly add up, especially in the AI context.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-an-api?u=76281980&t=125)** Gen AI is particularly expensive given the nature of the models.
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-an-api?u=76281980&t=129)** However, what's interesting is that the cost of Gen AI has been down, falling over 600 times from 2021 to March 2024 when this video was recorded.
>
> **[2:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-an-api?u=76281980&t=140)** These data points are for GPT-3 or ChatGPT equivalents.
>
> **[2:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-an-api?u=76281980&t=145)** These costs have been decreasing for a number of reasons.
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-an-api?u=76281980&t=148)** The cost of hardware has fallen, programs have gotten more optimized, and there's also a lot more investment money allowing companies to subsidize the cost of their APIs.
>
> **[2:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-an-api?u=76281980&t=157)** Now our next factor is latency.
>
> **[2:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-an-api?u=76281980&t=160)** When you have your use case figured out, it's always possible to run smaller and cheaper models, which might be cheaper than using an AI API.
>
> **[2:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-an-api?u=76281980&t=168)** Now smaller and custom models also benefit from lower latency.
>
> **[2:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-an-api?u=76281980&t=172)** Some applications require low millisecond latency like trading or recommendation systems.
>
> **[2:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-an-api?u=76281980&t=179)** And these latencies are infeasible with general APIs.
>
> **[3:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-an-api?u=76281980&t=182)** But for most use cases, especially in the Gen AI world, models like ChatGPT-3.5 are fast enough for most applications.
>
> **[3:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-an-api?u=76281980&t=190)** And in a globalized and multi-user world, we also need to consider multi-tenancy.
>
> **[3:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-an-api?u=76281980&t=195)** This is typically most important for B2B and international companies.
>
> **[3:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-an-api?u=76281980&t=199)** APIs might be geo-limited or have limits in organizational structure either for visibility or compliance.
>
> **[3:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-an-api?u=76281980&t=206)** So it's very important to understand how your application functions and how you'd integrate with these APIs.
>
> **[3:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-an-api?u=76281980&t=213)** As an example, some AI APIs have tenancy limits, meaning the number of dedicated applications that you provide to your users might be limited.
>
> **[3:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-an-api?u=76281980&t=222)** As a personal example, the company I work for, VoiceFlow, we had to manage a number of conversational AI applications for our customers.
>
> **[3:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-an-api?u=76281980&t=230)** At the beginning, we used a vendor API, but as we started to scale, the vendor API could no longer maintain our pace of growth.
>
> **[3:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-an-api?u=76281980&t=237)** So eventually we deployed an in-house model and system to deal with this.
>
> **[4:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-an-api?u=76281980&t=241)** So we used the vendor API to start and validate the problem and scaled with our own systems when we ran into issues, in our case, the vendor API took us through the tens of thousands of applications level, and we scaled ourselves through the hundreds of thousands.
>
> **[4:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-an-api?u=76281980&t=255)** Now this customizability might be really important to you, so it really depends on knowing your requirements.
>
> **[4:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-an-api?u=76281980&t=261)** Sometimes you might need to configure the API in a specific way that just is impossible.
>
> **[4:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-an-api?u=76281980&t=266)** Now overall, we've gone over these six factors.
>
> **[4:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-an-api?u=76281980&t=269)** Time to market, liability, cost, latency, multi-tenancy, and customizability.
>
> **[4:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-an-api?u=76281980&t=276)** All these are crucial for selecting the right AI API for your use case.
>
> **[4:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-an-api?u=76281980&t=281)** Now AI APIs are a great first option for accelerating your first AI implementation.
>
> **[4:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-an-api?u=76281980&t=286)** In the next video, we'll introduce you to AI as a platform, how it can be used for broader use cases.

> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-a-platform?u=76281980)

> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-a-platform?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] For many use cases, there isn't always an API for a task, so sometimes we need to build the models ourselves.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-a-platform?u=76281980&t=7)** In this case, it's smart to focus on the model and let a platform provide the structure that we need.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-a-platform?u=76281980&t=12)** In this video, we'll focus on the same parameters we used in the previous video for AI APIs, including time to market, reliability, cost, latency, multi-tenancy, and customizability.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-a-platform?u=76281980&t=26)** Platforms provide us with standardized methods to deploy and train models, allowing us to get to market faster for each subsequent model.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-a-platform?u=76281980&t=33)** Some of these frameworks include Databricks, SageMaker, Azure ML, Vertex AI, and many more.
>

>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-a-platform?u=76281980&t=48)** Cost-wise these platforms may be expensive, but many charge in the same elastic way as regular cloud services.
>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-a-platform?u=76281980&t=56)** As an example here, many of these platforms have pricing calculators as seen here for this Databricks one.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-a-platform?u=76281980&t=62)** Latency wise, different platforms have different capabilities such as more powerful hardware for faster inference, the ability to deploy on edge or enable streaming modes.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-a-platform?u=76281980&t=72)** As an example here, we have a screenshot from SageMaker.

>
> **[1:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-a-platform?u=76281980&t=87)** Now, many of these AI platforms are highly customizable, allowing you to choose the configurations that you need.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/introduction-to-ai-as-a-platform?u=76281980&t=94)** Sometimes, however, that's not enough.
>

#### Setup costs for AI APIs
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/setup-costs-for-ai-apis?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/setup-costs-for-ai-apis?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Let's discuss the setup costs when using AI APIs.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/setup-costs-for-ai-apis?u=76281980&t=4)** The powerful value of using AI APIs is avoiding traditional investments into large software purchases or hardware.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/setup-costs-for-ai-apis?u=76281980&t=12)** This allows companies to be more agile, makes technology more accessible for smaller teams or firms.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/setup-costs-for-ai-apis?u=76281980&t=19)** When working with APIs as a service, there may be discounts for upfront purchasing or certain billing commitments.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/setup-costs-for-ai-apis?u=76281980&t=26)** Now, not all AI APIs are elastic.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/setup-costs-for-ai-apis?u=76281980&t=29)** For certain larger contracts, you might be billed annually, which might impact your cash flow, and many enterprises choose to sign long-term contracts.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/setup-costs-for-ai-apis?u=76281980&t=37)** For example, a large European telecom signed a $1.5 billion contract over 10 years for AI services with a large cloud provider.
>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/setup-costs-for-ai-apis?u=76281980&t=47)** Because of the shift from set up costs to ongoing costs, we'll need to spend more time on the latter in our next video.

#### Ongoing costs for AI APIs
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ongoing-costs-for-ai-apis?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ongoing-costs-for-ai-apis?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Let's talk about the ongoing costs of using an AI API.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ongoing-costs-for-ai-apis?u=76281980&t=4)** There are three main ways to consume an AI API.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ongoing-costs-for-ai-apis?u=76281980&t=7)** The first one is managed hosting.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ongoing-costs-for-ai-apis?u=76281980&t=10)** The second is per API consumption.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ongoing-costs-for-ai-apis?u=76281980&t=12)** And the third one is a defined plan.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ongoing-costs-for-ai-apis?u=76281980&t=15)** Managed hosting is more traditional from a cloud perspective, where you pay a vendor to host a model and pay by the hour.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ongoing-costs-for-ai-apis?u=76281980&t=22)** Even though it's managed hosting, you can still connect easily via API.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ongoing-costs-for-ai-apis?u=76281980&t=26)** These hosting models are good if you have consistent workloads.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ongoing-costs-for-ai-apis?u=76281980&t=30)** Now as an example, between two vendors on the left here, we have AWS Bedrock serving pre-trained Llama with both one month and six-month commitments.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ongoing-costs-for-ai-apis?u=76281980&t=38)** And with [Together.AI](https://Together.AI), you pay by model size per hour.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ongoing-costs-for-ai-apis?u=76281980&t=43)** Our second option is per API consumption pricing or serverless pricing.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ongoing-costs-for-ai-apis?u=76281980&t=48)** Here we pay by API call with some additional parameters like tokens that are used.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ongoing-costs-for-ai-apis?u=76281980&t=54)** We connected these models via an API, so it's still easy to use.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ongoing-costs-for-ai-apis?u=76281980&t=58)** And these are great for elastic workloads where you're not sure how much of a model you're going to use at a given time.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ongoing-costs-for-ai-apis?u=76281980&t=64)** Two examples of this pricing structure include the Google Translate pricing, where it costs $20 per million characters; or the ChatGPT pricing where it costs per input and output tokens.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ongoing-costs-for-ai-apis?u=76281980&t=76)** Now, diving more into the ChatGPT pricing, tokens are worth approximately a 1,000 tokens to 750 words.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ongoing-costs-for-ai-apis?u=76281980&t=84)** And we can see here that output tokens are around three times as expensive as input tokens, meaning that the context you pass into an LLM is cheaper than the output that you generate.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ongoing-costs-for-ai-apis?u=76281980&t=94)** Now, if we were to send a million input tokens and a million output tokens were generated, it cost us roughly 50 cents for the input and a $1.05 for the output.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ongoing-costs-for-ai-apis?u=76281980&t=104)** Note that these prices are for March, 2024, but the key concepts will remain the same.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ongoing-costs-for-ai-apis?u=76281980&t=110)** Now the third option is plan-based pricing.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ongoing-costs-for-ai-apis?u=76281980&t=113)** In this case, for a dedicated plan, you pay per month.
>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ongoing-costs-for-ai-apis?u=76281980&t=116)** Now looking at the [stability.ai](https://stability.ai) platform, you can see that their pricing is based on membership.
>
> **[2:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ongoing-costs-for-ai-apis?u=76281980&t=122)** You pay per month, and you gain different capabilities based on non-commercial, professional or enterprise needs.
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ongoing-costs-for-ai-apis?u=76281980&t=129)** On top of this, you purchase credits to actually use on the models.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ongoing-costs-for-ai-apis?u=76281980&t=133)** What's interesting is when I was planning this video, the pricing was actually a little bit different, matching credits to plan types.
>
> **[2:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ongoing-costs-for-ai-apis?u=76281980&t=140)** This is just another indicator that pricing can change at any point in time, so it's important to understand the key concepts and not the pricing itself.
>
> **[2:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ongoing-costs-for-ai-apis?u=76281980&t=150)** Now, for those of you who have worked at enterprise companies, you might know that the enterprise tier usually has custom pricing, meaning it's very hard to figure out at first how much something costs.
>
> **[2:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ongoing-costs-for-ai-apis?u=76281980&t=160)** This might include minimum spend, hourly consumption, API pricing or more.
>
> **[2:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ongoing-costs-for-ai-apis?u=76281980&t=165)** Now, even though we've talked about three different pricing plans, all of these are for APIs that are easy to use.
>
> **[2:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ongoing-costs-for-ai-apis?u=76281980&t=172)** All you have to do is create an API key and you can start consuming the model.
>
> **[2:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ongoing-costs-for-ai-apis?u=76281980&t=177)** And with that, we've covered the three different types of pricing models that exist for AI APIs.
>
> **[3:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ongoing-costs-for-ai-apis?u=76281980&t=182)** In the next video, we'll go into an example on estimating the cost of a translation feature, working in Excel to put the numbers together.

>
> **[2:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-what-is-rag?u=76281980&t=168)** We'll then search the vector database and retrieve the most similar chunks from our documentation.
>
> **[2:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-what-is-rag?u=76281980&t=174)** And finally, we'll use that to be our context that we pass into our large-language model.

> **[2:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-what-is-rag?u=76281980&t=179)** So our context in a large-language model will look like this.
>
> **[3:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-what-is-rag?u=76281980&t=183)** Similar to what we showed earlier, we'll have context, the information that we found, and then our question.
>
> **[3:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-what-is-rag?u=76281980&t=189)** Now that we know how RAG works, we're going to figure out the price and costs of this type of solution.

#### Estimating cost for a RAG solution: Costs of RAG
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-costs-of-rag?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-costs-of-rag?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] In this video, we're going to learn how to price a RAG solution.

> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-costs-of-rag?u=76281980&t=4)** In the last video, we learned about the different components of RAG, including the embedding model, the vector database, and the large language model.

> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-costs-of-rag?u=76281980&t=17)** So let's head over to our exercise files and click on 02_07 under chapter two.

>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-costs-of-rag?u=76281980&t=24)** At the top, we have some miscellaneous variables, as we saw earlier, and then we get into the two parts, uploading data and running our bot.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-costs-of-rag?u=76281980&t=34)** Let's start off with uploading data.
>

>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-costs-of-rag?u=76281980&t=42)** We're going to split these documents on average into chunks of 300.
>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-costs-of-rag?u=76281980&t=47)** So in total we're going to have around 1,667 vectors, which are one-to-one to chunks.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-costs-of-rag?u=76281980&t=54)** We can see that here in our formula.
>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-costs-of-rag?u=76281980&t=56)** Now, we need to embed all these different chunks into their vectors.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-costs-of-rag?u=76281980&t=60)** We can calculate that by taking our documents and multiplying them by the tokens per document.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-costs-of-rag?u=76281980&t=67)** This will give us 500,000.
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-costs-of-rag?u=76281980&t=69)** This is typically how embedding models are priced.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-costs-of-rag?u=76281980&t=72)** Next up, we add the vector DB initial costs.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-costs-of-rag?u=76281980&t=75)** So depending on which vector database that you're using, sometimes it costs to upload data.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-costs-of-rag?u=76281980&t=80)** In this case, the pricing model that we're using doesn't have an initial cost, so we've written it down as zero.
>
> **[1:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-costs-of-rag?u=76281980&t=87)** In the next portion we have the vector size.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-costs-of-rag?u=76281980&t=89)** I just have this information here because depending on the solution that you use, you might be charged by the vector size for your vector DB.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-costs-of-rag?u=76281980&t=97)** Now finally, let's go through the embedding cost.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-costs-of-rag?u=76281980&t=101)** Embedding costs are actually pretty low.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-costs-of-rag?u=76281980&t=103)** So per million tokens, as of this recording of March, 2024, it costs about 2 cents to embed a million tokens using OpenAI's version three small embedding model.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-costs-of-rag?u=76281980&t=114)** So our total embedding cost comes up to 1 cent.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-costs-of-rag?u=76281980&t=118)** Now this is pretty cheap, and through my experience working at Voiceflow where we use a lot of RAG applications, this is pretty accurate in practice as well.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-costs-of-rag?u=76281980&t=126)** Now, let's scroll down to part two of running the bot.
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-costs-of-rag?u=76281980&t=129)** This is where most of the prices come in.
>
> **[2:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-costs-of-rag?u=76281980&t=132)** So let's start off with the first section up here.
>
> **[2:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-costs-of-rag?u=76281980&t=135)** We're going to assume that we get a thousand questions per month, and each question is going to be 50 tokens long.
>
> **[2:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-costs-of-rag?u=76281980&t=142)** So embedding these questions is actually going to be very cheap, in this case, showing close to zero.
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-costs-of-rag?u=76281980&t=148)** And we got this by multiplying the number of questions by the length of the question and then figuring out the pricing per million tokens.
>
> **[2:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-costs-of-rag?u=76281980&t=157)** Now we're going to assume that to actually serve our chatbot, we fall into a free tier of application.
>
> **[2:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-costs-of-rag?u=76281980&t=162)** So we put a cost of zero.
>
> **[2:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-costs-of-rag?u=76281980&t=164)** Now, for a vector DB, we're going to assume that we're going to be running this in a high availability mode, and each of these pods, which we're running our vector DB in, we're going to cost $25 per month.
>
> **[2:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-costs-of-rag?u=76281980&t=176)** In this last section, let's talk about the LLM portion.
>
> **[3:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-costs-of-rag?u=76281980&t=180)** So we're going to assume that our average response length is a hundred tokens.
>
> **[3:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-costs-of-rag?u=76281980&t=184)** As we know it's important to separate response and input lengths because they cost different amounts.
>
> **[3:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-costs-of-rag?u=76281980&t=190)** We're going to assume we retrieve five chunks per vector search.
>
> **[3:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-costs-of-rag?u=76281980&t=194)** So in total, our average context length is going to be 1500, which is 300 total vectors multiplied by five.
>
> **[3:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-costs-of-rag?u=76281980&t=203)** And we can calculate our total input tokens by taking the number of questions that we have by the average context length, and we get 1.5 million.
>
> **[3:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-costs-of-rag?u=76281980&t=213)** And we can do the same thing with our output tokens.
>
> **[3:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-costs-of-rag?u=76281980&t=216)** We take the number of questions per month and multiply it by the average response length, so we get 100,000.
>
> **[3:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-costs-of-rag?u=76281980&t=223)** Now for our LLM costs, I'm using the March, 2024 pricing for ChatGPT.
>
> **[3:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-costs-of-rag?u=76281980&t=228)** So that's 50 cents per million input tokens and 1.5 dollars per output token.
>
> **[3:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-costs-of-rag?u=76281980&t=236)** I'm going to multiply our usage by the cost and get 75 cents per month for our LLM input costs and 15 cents per month for LLM output costs.
>
> **[4:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-costs-of-rag?u=76281980&t=246)** Now in total we have 90 cents for our LLMs and $75 for the rest, which includes our vector DB and embedding model, and our total costs are $75.91.
>
> **[4:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-costs-of-rag?u=76281980&t=260)** So as you can see here, our vector DB is consuming the most amount of money for running this application, and we can go ahead and expand to other scenarios.
>
> **[4:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/estimating-cost-for-a-rag-solution-costs-of-rag?u=76281980&t=270)** Click the right and hit unhide.

#### Solution: Estimating the cost of a book summarization
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-estimating-the-cost-of-a-book-summarization?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-estimating-the-cost-of-a-book-summarization?u=76281980&t=0)** (upbeat electronic music)
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-estimating-the-cost-of-a-book-summarization?u=76281980&t=5)** - [Instructor] So let's go through a solution to this problem.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-estimating-the-cost-of-a-book-summarization?u=76281980&t=8)** I've divided our spreadsheet into three main sections: Miscellaneous values, Initial Costs, and Monthly Costs.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-estimating-the-cost-of-a-book-summarization?u=76281980&t=16)** Let's start off with Initial Costs, since we have our main assumptions there.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-estimating-the-cost-of-a-book-summarization?u=76281980&t=21)** We're assuming that we have 500,000 books in our library with 100,000 words on average per book.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-estimating-the-cost-of-a-book-summarization?u=76281980&t=27)** We're aiming to translate to five different languages and have three different types of summaries, for plot, themes, and character.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-estimating-the-cost-of-a-book-summarization?u=76281980&t=34)** Each of our summaries are going to be around 100 words.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-estimating-the-cost-of-a-book-summarization?u=76281980&t=37)** So to calculate our initial input tokens, we're going to take our initial number of books, multiply it by the number of words per book.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-estimating-the-cost-of-a-book-summarization?u=76281980&t=46)** We're then going to multiply it by tokens per word.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-estimating-the-cost-of-a-book-summarization?u=76281980&t=49)** That's how we end up with 62.5 billion tokens.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-estimating-the-cost-of-a-book-summarization?u=76281980&t=53)** Now, for output tokens, we're going to do something similar.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-estimating-the-cost-of-a-book-summarization?u=76281980&t=57)** We're going to take the initial number of books, multiply it by the number of languages, multiply it by the type of summaries we want to do, and by our length.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-estimating-the-cost-of-a-book-summarization?u=76281980&t=66)** We're then going to multiply it by the tokens per word.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-estimating-the-cost-of-a-book-summarization?u=76281980&t=70)** Now, let's get to this cost number.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-estimating-the-cost-of-a-book-summarization?u=76281980&t=72)** We chose Claude 2 as our model for scenario one.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-estimating-the-cost-of-a-book-summarization?u=76281980&t=76)** Claude 2 has a context length of 200,000, meaning that it can fit our books into its whole context length.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-estimating-the-cost-of-a-book-summarization?u=76281980&t=82)** Claude 2 costs $8 per million input tokens and $24 per million output tokens.
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-estimating-the-cost-of-a-book-summarization?u=76281980&t=88)** So calculating our total initial cost, we take the cost per input token and multiply it by the number of input tokens.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-estimating-the-cost-of-a-book-summarization?u=76281980&t=97)** And then we add the number of output tokens and multiply it by the cost per output tokens.
>
> **[1:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-estimating-the-cost-of-a-book-summarization?u=76281980&t=102)** We then divide it by a million.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-estimating-the-cost-of-a-book-summarization?u=76281980&t=105)** As a result, we get half a million dollars as our initial costs.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-estimating-the-cost-of-a-book-summarization?u=76281980&t=109)** That's pretty pricey.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-estimating-the-cost-of-a-book-summarization?u=76281980&t=111)** Now, scrolling down into our monthly costs, we're going to assume that we're going to add 1,000 new books per month.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-estimating-the-cost-of-a-book-summarization?u=76281980&t=117)** Using the same formula, we calculate our input tokens and our output tokens.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-estimating-the-cost-of-a-book-summarization?u=76281980&t=123)** So we get a cost of around $1,000 a month.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-estimating-the-cost-of-a-book-summarization?u=76281980&t=126)** If we do this for two months, our costs will be $524,590.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-estimating-the-cost-of-a-book-summarization?u=76281980&t=133)** Now let's unhide scenario number two.
>
> **[2:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-estimating-the-cost-of-a-book-summarization?u=76281980&t=135)** So for scenario number two, we used ChatGPT 3.5.
>
> **[2:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-estimating-the-cost-of-a-book-summarization?u=76281980&t=139)** It has a context length of 128,000 tokens, which should be fine for this application.
>
> **[2:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-estimating-the-cost-of-a-book-summarization?u=76281980&t=145)** ChatGPT 3.5 is much cheaper, costing 50 cents per million input tokens and $1.5 for a million output tokens.
>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-estimating-the-cost-of-a-book-summarization?u=76281980&t=153)** As a result, the initial total cost is around $32,656.
>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-estimating-the-cost-of-a-book-summarization?u=76281980&t=159)** And the cost per month is around $42.
>
> **[2:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-estimating-the-cost-of-a-book-summarization?u=76281980&t=163)** Now below, I've graphed out these two figures.
>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-estimating-the-cost-of-a-book-summarization?u=76281980&t=166)** You can see here that ChatGPT is significantly cheaper than Claude 2.
>
> **[2:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-estimating-the-cost-of-a-book-summarization?u=76281980&t=171)** That's a sample solution to our library question.
>
> **[2:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-estimating-the-cost-of-a-book-summarization?u=76281980&t=173)** In this challenge, we took our knowledge from the chapter and learned how to estimate the cost of a complex problem.
>
> **[2:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-estimating-the-cost-of-a-book-summarization?u=76281980&t=179)** In the next chapter, we're going to dive into the pricing of the major AI vendors so we can figure out how to do better estimates for more models.

> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/diving-into-google-ai-pricing?u=76281980&t=36)** In this case, you'll notice that text is charged by every thousand characters, which is different than the other models we've seen that charge by token.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/diving-into-google-ai-pricing?u=76281980&t=45)** And looking at the pricing, we can see here that the text input is quite cheap.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/diving-into-google-ai-pricing?u=76281980&t=51)** If we multiply this by 1000, we'll see that Gemini Pro is priced at 12 cents per million characters, which is roughly 40 to 50 cents per token, depending on the language.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/diving-into-google-ai-pricing?u=76281980&t=62)** And this is roughly the same price as ChatGPT.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/diving-into-google-ai-pricing?u=76281980&t=65)** Now for output, we can see that it's three times as expensive, meaning that it costs around 37 cents per million characters, or $1 to 1.5 per million tokens, also comparable to ChatGPT.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/diving-into-google-ai-pricing?u=76281980&t=78)** Now, if we go to an example we talked about before, which is a standard RAG response, Gemini Pro would cost around 0.1 of a cent, depending on the length.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/diving-into-google-ai-pricing?u=76281980&t=86)** If we go back to the context of summarizing a book, it'd cost around 10 cents.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/diving-into-google-ai-pricing?u=76281980&t=92)** And in a multilingual context, Gemini Pro would likely be cheaper than ChatGPT 3.5, given the way that the character pricing interacts with different languages.
>
> **[1:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/diving-into-google-ai-pricing?u=76281980&t=102)** Now, the nice thing about Gemini Pro is that it's similar to GPT-4 in the sense that it can accept multimodal inputs.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/diving-into-google-ai-pricing?u=76281980&t=109)** As you can see here, the image input is priced per image and the video input is priced by second.
>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/diving-into-google-ai-pricing?u=76281980&t=116)** Images with Gemini are cheaper to use if they're high resolution and more expensive than GPT-4 Vision if they are low resolution.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/diving-into-google-ai-pricing?u=76281980&t=123)** Let's scroll down and go to the next section, which is image-based models.
>
> **[2:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/diving-into-google-ai-pricing?u=76281980&t=127)** As you can see here by pricing, most of the prices are based per image, similar to what we've seen with Stable Diffusion and DALL-E.
>
> **[2:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/diving-into-google-ai-pricing?u=76281980&t=136)** We also have the opportunity to fine tune a model, and here we're charged per hour.
>
> **[2:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/diving-into-google-ai-pricing?u=76281980&t=141)** We can dive deeper into this pricing, but that's beyond the scope of this video.
>
> **[2:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/diving-into-google-ai-pricing?u=76281980&t=145)** Now let's keep scrolling down.
>
> **[2:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/diving-into-google-ai-pricing?u=76281980&t=147)** We can see here we have multimodal embeddings.
>
> **[2:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/diving-into-google-ai-pricing?u=76281980&t=150)** These are similar to the embeddings offered by OpenAI, but they also have multimodal capabilities, meaning you can embed text, image, video altogether in one set of embeddings.
>
> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/diving-into-google-ai-pricing?u=76281980&t=161)** This capability would allow you to create a RAG application that retrieves video, image, text, and generates the response all at once.

>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/overview-of-technical-components-and-tooling?u=76281980&t=7)** In this chapter we'll cover the landscape of training tools.

>

>

>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/overview-of-technical-components-and-tooling?u=76281980&t=61)** We also need to pre-process it from raw sources, needing a transformation pipeline.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/overview-of-technical-components-and-tooling?u=76281980&t=66)** We should also monitor our training and sort the models and revisions somewhere.

> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/overview-of-technical-components-and-tooling?u=76281980&t=71)** And finally, we need a team to manage all these different components.
>

>

>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/setting-up-an-ai-training-cluster?u=76281980&t=50)** Now, the reason that GPUs are typically talked about is because there's a large software suite available for them.

>

>

>

>

>
> **[2:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/setting-up-an-ai-training-cluster?u=76281980&t=143)** These are used to fine-tune models or even train models from scratch.
>
> **[2:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/setting-up-an-ai-training-cluster?u=76281980&t=147)** These clusters are currently highly in demand and require pre-reservation.
>
> **[2:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/setting-up-an-ai-training-cluster?u=76281980&t=152)** And for these clusters, the cost would be around $1000 a day.
>

#### Cost of compute for training AI models
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/cost-of-compute-for-training-ai-models?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/cost-of-compute-for-training-ai-models?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] In the last video, we learned that GPUs and other accelerators are essential to our model training.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/cost-of-compute-for-training-ai-models?u=76281980&t=6)** But is that all that we need?
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/cost-of-compute-for-training-ai-models?u=76281980&t=9)** Just like we need RAM, CPU, and disk for day-to-day operations, model training requires us to have sufficient resources to transfer the task to the GPUs.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/cost-of-compute-for-training-ai-models?u=76281980&t=19)** Here's an example of the cycle of training a model.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/cost-of-compute-for-training-ai-models?u=76281980&t=23)** We can see here, first, you have to open your files, then read them into memory, send the request to train to the GPU, and repeat the cycle.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/cost-of-compute-for-training-ai-models?u=76281980&t=31)** Now, this process can be changed, optimized, and arranged differently, but we still need these key compute components.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/cost-of-compute-for-training-ai-models?u=76281980&t=38)** Now, you might be wondering, just how much CPU, memory, and disk do we need?
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/cost-of-compute-for-training-ai-models?u=76281980&t=44)** Well, the minimum is typically to run some kind of training program, which includes the Python and the data.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/cost-of-compute-for-training-ai-models?u=76281980&t=49)** But generally, we don't have to worry about this.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/cost-of-compute-for-training-ai-models?u=76281980&t=52)** Cloud providers bundle CPU, RAM, disk, and GPUs together usually.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/cost-of-compute-for-training-ai-models?u=76281980&t=57)** For example, if we want to run an AWS A100 cluster, we'd already be given 96 CPUs, over a terabyte of RAM, and eight terabytes of disk.
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/cost-of-compute-for-training-ai-models?u=76281980&t=69)** So in this case, these resources are already pre-assigned to us.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/cost-of-compute-for-training-ai-models?u=76281980&t=72)** Now, in a more customizable model, for example, on GCP, you might want to deploy a T4 GPU.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/cost-of-compute-for-training-ai-models?u=76281980&t=78)** This would require an N1 VM type, which needs to have at least one CPU and two gigabytes of RAM.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/cost-of-compute-for-training-ai-models?u=76281980&t=86)** Now, typically, you'd want to deploy a little bit more, so getting an N1-standard-2 would cost around $60 a month.
>
> **[1:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/cost-of-compute-for-training-ai-models?u=76281980&t=93)** Now that we know the training requirements that we need for both GPUs and other compute resources, we'll talk about the data processing side.

>

>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/data-movement-and-storage?u=76281980&t=6)** First, we need to make sure that we're collecting the right type of data.

>

>

>

>
> **[3:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/data-movement-and-storage?u=76281980&t=221)** That might cost you around $90 per terabyte.

> **[3:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/data-movement-and-storage?u=76281980&t=223)** This constant transfer might add up as you're training the model and constantly pulling and pushing data apart.
>
> **[3:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/data-movement-and-storage?u=76281980&t=230)** Now, if your data strategy involves storing data in a data warehouse, accessing this quantity of data might cost hundreds of dollars per query, so make sure you understand how this data is going to be used.
>
> **[4:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/data-movement-and-storage?u=76281980&t=242)** Now, thankfully, training jobs are batch based, meaning that the data that you're using is typically versioned and fixed.
>
> **[4:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/data-movement-and-storage?u=76281980&t=250)** So this means this is typically cheaper than streaming jobs or other types of use cases.

>

>
> **[4:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/data-movement-and-storage?u=76281980&t=266)** Now the real cost comes with transformation.

> **[4:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/data-movement-and-storage?u=76281980&t=269)** Now, let's say you're processing a data set, like Common Crawl, you might need to clean it since it comes from the raw internet.
>
> **[4:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/data-movement-and-storage?u=76281980&t=275)** This might include removing duplicates, filtering with some heuristics, or removing content that is inappropriate.
>
> **[4:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/data-movement-and-storage?u=76281980&t=282)** You might also do transformations, like joining different data sets, or validating that data has certain consistency, like the review ratings matching the review text.
>
> **[4:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/data-movement-and-storage?u=76281980&t=291)** You might also want to run through some smaller models to help label and categorize the data.
>
> **[4:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/data-movement-and-storage?u=76281980&t=297)** With all these transformations, you start getting into the big data space and it becomes expensive to pay for all these compute or services that accomplish this.
>
> **[5:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/data-movement-and-storage?u=76281980&t=307)** Now, since we're doing batch transformations, we don't have to worry about streaming, unless you're going to do something like continuous retraining, which is a pretty advanced technique.
>
> **[5:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/data-movement-and-storage?u=76281980&t=316)** So these are the costs of storing and transforming data in an AI context.
>
> **[5:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/data-movement-and-storage?u=76281980&t=321)** In the next video, we're going to talk about AI model iterations and evaluations, since you likely won't just train one version of a model.
