>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-model-training-iteration-and-evaluation?u=76281980&t=106)** In this space, experimentation and ideation often blur.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-model-training-iteration-and-evaluation?u=76281980&t=110)** It's hard to figure out if a model works or not without actually experimenting, so this is typically a cycle.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-model-training-iteration-and-evaluation?u=76281980&t=117)** For experimentation, you typically want to run 10 to 1,000 experiments depending on the model complexity.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-model-training-iteration-and-evaluation?u=76281980&t=124)** The more complex the model, the more iterations you need to run.
>
> **[2:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-model-training-iteration-and-evaluation?u=76281980&t=127)** Or in other words, there's a higher risk of failure because you might not get to the correct idea in time.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-model-training-iteration-and-evaluation?u=76281980&t=133)** Now, let's assume that you've chosen the right model architecture, you have clean data, are you done?
>
> **[2:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-model-training-iteration-and-evaluation?u=76281980&t=139)** Probably not.
>
> **[2:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-model-training-iteration-and-evaluation?u=76281980&t=140)** For a lot of models, we do something called hyper parameter tuning.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-model-training-iteration-and-evaluation?u=76281980&t=144)** Hyper parameters are things outside the actual model, and they help guide the model to learn a better behavior.
>
> **[2:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-model-training-iteration-and-evaluation?u=76281980&t=150)** Here's an example of what this might look like.
>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-model-training-iteration-and-evaluation?u=76281980&t=153)** We might choose hyper parameters like batch size, dropout, the number of epochs, and the learning rate, and we might iterate over them to get the model to have the lowest loss.
>
> **[2:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-model-training-iteration-and-evaluation?u=76281980&t=163)** In this visualization from weights and biases, you can see here that there are several iterations, and in practice, there might be thousands depending on the number of hyper parameters.
>
> **[2:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-model-training-iteration-and-evaluation?u=76281980&t=172)** Now, finally, you might get to a model that seems to be doing quite well.
>
> **[2:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-model-training-iteration-and-evaluation?u=76281980&t=176)** You now need to go through the evaluation stage.
>
> **[2:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-model-training-iteration-and-evaluation?u=76281980&t=179)** Evaluation is running models on test sets, data that's never been seen before.
>
> **[3:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-model-training-iteration-and-evaluation?u=76281980&t=184)** Some of these test sets are well-known.
>
> **[3:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-model-training-iteration-and-evaluation?u=76281980&t=186)** If you've been keeping up with the large language model papers, you'll see many of these benchmarks are reported on frequently, such as MMLU.
>
> **[3:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-model-training-iteration-and-evaluation?u=76281980&t=194)** Now, the challenge with many models, especially GenAI models, is that there might be data contamination.
>
> **[3:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-model-training-iteration-and-evaluation?u=76281980&t=200)** Test sets might end up in your training sets, leading to misleading results.
>
> **[3:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-model-training-iteration-and-evaluation?u=76281980&t=205)** As an example, in the GPT-4 technical report, they dedicate a section to explain how contaminated GPT-4 might be.
>
> **[3:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-model-training-iteration-and-evaluation?u=76281980&t=212)** In this case, they measure contamination by checking for exact matches or very close matches in the model outputs.
>
> **[3:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-model-training-iteration-and-evaluation?u=76281980&t=220)** Now, these techniques aren't perfect, but they're a great way to figure out if your model's just memorizing training data or can it actually provide interesting results.
>
> **[3:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-model-training-iteration-and-evaluation?u=76281980&t=228)** And many companies have their own proprietary evaluation sets, especially if their domains are quite secretive, or they have sensitive information like healthcare or finance.
>
> **[3:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-model-training-iteration-and-evaluation?u=76281980&t=238)** Now going back to our model training pipeline, we can see here that to make a model successful, we have to go through all these different steps.
>
> **[4:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-model-training-iteration-and-evaluation?u=76281980&t=245)** And what we need to realize is managing an AI project is different than software.
>
> **[4:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-model-training-iteration-and-evaluation?u=76281980&t=250)** There are many opportunities for things to go wrong or for us to reevaluate.
>
> **[4:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-model-training-iteration-and-evaluation?u=76281980&t=254)** As a general recommendation, budget 10 to 100 times the amount of time and money you think a successful model run will take.
>
> **[4:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-model-training-iteration-and-evaluation?u=76281980&t=262)** There's a lot of uncertainty in AI model training, so you need to make sure that the team has adequate time to do so.
>
> **[4:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-model-training-iteration-and-evaluation?u=76281980&t=267)** So in the next video, we'll talk about tracking these experiments with logging, monitoring, and storage since we know that this process can be quite complex.

#### Fine-tuning models
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/fine-tuning-models?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/fine-tuning-models?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] As we've talked about in this chapter, training AI models from scratch can be expensive.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/fine-tuning-models?u=76281980&t=4)** So what if I told you there's a technique to save time and money and keep the same accuracy for these types of models?
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/fine-tuning-models?u=76281980&t=12)** We'd also need less data to accomplish this task.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/fine-tuning-models?u=76281980&t=15)** So I'd like to introduce you to the concept of fine tuning.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/fine-tuning-models?u=76281980&t=18)** We can fine tune existing models to save up to 99% of the costs to accomplish a task.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/fine-tuning-models?u=76281980&t=24)** So how do we do this?
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/fine-tuning-models?u=76281980&t=25)** First, we should find an open source model for our task.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/fine-tuning-models?u=76281980&t=28)** Afterwards, we can take our model and our new data, train them together and get a fine tuned model.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/fine-tuning-models?u=76281980&t=35)** As a specific example, let's say we've been using LLaMa for some of our experiments.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/fine-tuning-models?u=76281980&t=41)** It's doing quite well, but we want to improve the performance for banking specific tasks.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/fine-tuning-models?u=76281980&t=45)** So what we can do is we can fine tune LLaMa with banking data and get a variation like banking LLaMa.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/fine-tuning-models?u=76281980&t=51)** So let's go through some costs to fine tune.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/fine-tuning-models?u=76281980&t=54)** Here I have two different models for two different types of tasks.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/fine-tuning-models?u=76281980&t=57)** The first one is I'm taking Bert, which is an open source model, and I'm going to fine tune it for sentiment analysis.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/fine-tuning-models?u=76281980&t=64)** I'm going to use the IMDB sentiment dataset, and I'm going to do full fine tuning.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/fine-tuning-models?u=76281980&t=70)** I'm going to use a T4 graphics card, and this task takes around 60 minutes and around 68 cents.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/fine-tuning-models?u=76281980&t=76)** I got this information from a lightning AI tutorial.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/fine-tuning-models?u=76281980&t=78)** Now the second model is we want to fine tune LLaMa2 to be more conversational.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/fine-tuning-models?u=76281980&t=84)** We can use a dataset like Databricks Dolly and use a technique called QLoRa and fine tune on an A10G, which on AWS is called MLG5 for xlarge.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/fine-tuning-models?u=76281980&t=95)** Now this will take around 8.8 hours and cost around $18.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/fine-tuning-models?u=76281980&t=99)** I got this information from a technical lead who wrote a blog post on Hugging Face.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/fine-tuning-models?u=76281980&t=104)** So you can see here that there are different techniques that you can actually use.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/fine-tuning-models?u=76281980&t=108)** So let's dive into them.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/fine-tuning-models?u=76281980&t=109)** The first technique is a full fine tuning where we take the data and we train the whole model that we've actually used, so the whole model becomes adapted to this task.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/fine-tuning-models?u=76281980&t=118)** The second technique we can use is we can only use partial layers, meaning we freeze the layers of earlier models and only apply the data to later ones.
>
> **[2:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/fine-tuning-models?u=76281980&t=128)** This technique actually works quite well.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/fine-tuning-models?u=76281980&t=130)** The final technique that's become more common recently is called Parameter Efficient Tuning.
>
> **[2:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/fine-tuning-models?u=76281980&t=135)** One of these techniques has become incredibly popular in the industry called LoRa, where you train an adapter on the side and only adjust the parameters in that adapter, and afterwards, you either have the choice of keeping the adapter on the side and running the two models together or merging it back into the original model.
>
> **[2:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/fine-tuning-models?u=76281980&t=154)** So fine tuning is a great way to save time and money.
>
> **[2:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/fine-tuning-models?u=76281980&t=157)** Now, we've talked about the different techniques and tools that we can use for training models, but you need someone to do that.
>
> **[2:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/fine-tuning-models?u=76281980&t=164)** In the next video, we'll talk about hiring the team to train our AI models.

>

#### Solution: Training AI for your enterprise

>

>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-training-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=36)** Now on B6, this is a hyper parameter, figuring out how many layers we're going to fine tune.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-training-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=40)** In this case, I'm assuming we're going to fine tune the whole model.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-training-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=44)** And finally on B7 is the number of epochs we're going to train for.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-training-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=48)** An epoch is a single pass of all the data, meaning five epochs is passing through all the data five times.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-training-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=55)** Now in B9, we have an all-inclusive cost for GPU, CPU, RAM and disc.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-training-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=60)** We're assuming we're using a T4 graphics card, and these are the average cloud costs.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-training-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=64)** Now, based on the number of layers we have, the graphics card we're using, and the number of epochs, I've calculated our time to fine tuning, which is around 500 minutes.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-training-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=74)** I've also added five minutes for boot up time to get all this infrastructure started.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-training-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=79)** In multiplying our cost per hour on B9 by our total time on B12, we're going to get our total cost per model run, which is around $5.89.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-training-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=91)** Now in practice, this might vary.
>
> **[1:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-training-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=93)** We're using this as a reasonable assumption.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-training-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=96)** Now let's head over to the right side of the spreadsheet.
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-training-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=98)** I'm going to start off in column G and H.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-training-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=101)** In these two columns, we make assumptions on our team structure.
>

>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-training-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=108)** Each engineer is going to cost us around 250,000 per year, and the project is going to last two months.
>

> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-training-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=119)** At the top, we have our tooling.
>
> **[2:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-training-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=122)** I've assumed that our experiment tracking is going to cost around $150 per person per month.
>
> **[2:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-training-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=128)** This is higher than the $50 we saw earlier, but we're an enterprise, so likely it's going to cost more for the additional features.
>
> **[2:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-training-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=136)** Now, in E3, I've included an internal chargeback.
>
> **[2:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-training-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=140)** Internal chargeback is when one team in a company charges another team for its services.
>
> **[2:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-training-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=145)** So we might not manage the data tools that we need, but we should be paying for our share based on another team's expenses.
>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-training-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=153)** So I've estimated that to be around $10,000 per month.
>
> **[2:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-training-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=156)** Next, on E4, I estimate that we'll run around 100 experiments to validate that our data is working well and to choose the correct model, the number of Brit-based models, as well as other data validations that we can run.
>
> **[2:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-training-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=169)** We're estimating that'll be around 100 times.
>
> **[2:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-training-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=172)** After we validated our model and our data set, we're going to go ahead and run our hyper parameter tuning.
>
> **[2:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-training-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=178)** We estimate we're going to do this 50 times.
>
> **[3:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-training-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=180)** Now to add up all these costs, we're going to have $10,000 per month, taking into account the chargeback and the experiment tracking.
>
> **[3:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-training-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=189)** Our training costs will be around $883 based on the number of experiments that we're doing and our final hyper parameter runs.
>
> **[3:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-training-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=197)** And finally, we have our total labor costs, multiplying our team size by the yearly rate, and then multiplying by the number of months our project will take.
>
> **[3:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-training-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=206)** So this total cost will be around $188,000.
>
> **[3:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-training-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=210)** So I'm going to ask my manager for $200,000 to complete this project.
>
> **[3:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-training-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=214)** Now, the difference between the total cost and the budget ask are quite small.
>
> **[3:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-training-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=218)** The reason for this is that in our project length, I've actually doubled the capacity that I think that it would take to run this project.
>
> **[3:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-training-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=225)** So we have some buffer estimated in, just in case anything goes wrong on the modeling side, data side, or final business objectives.
>
> **[3:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-training-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=233)** So through the sample solution, we've learned how to estimate model costs, labor costs, and additional tooling, and make a concrete ask for delivering this project.

### 5. Costs of Hosting AI

#### Hosting and running your AI models
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hosting-and-running-your-ai-models?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hosting-and-running-your-ai-models?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] You have an AI model.
>
> **[0:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hosting-and-running-your-ai-models?u=76281980&t=2)** Now what?
>
> **[0:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hosting-and-running-your-ai-models?u=76281980&t=2)** In this video and chapter, we'll be talking about the key components of hosting and deploying AI models.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hosting-and-running-your-ai-models?u=76281980&t=9)** We'll talk about three main things in this chapter, the challenges of deploying models, choosing the right hardware and predicting costs.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hosting-and-running-your-ai-models?u=76281980&t=17)** So why is deploying an AI model challenging?
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hosting-and-running-your-ai-models?u=76281980&t=19)** There are six main reasons.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hosting-and-running-your-ai-models?u=76281980&t=21)** Many of these are similar to the ones we talked about in the training chapter.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hosting-and-running-your-ai-models?u=76281980&t=26)** Starting off, we have the differences between the research and production environment.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hosting-and-running-your-ai-models?u=76281980&t=30)** Sometimes this is a hardware difference.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hosting-and-running-your-ai-models?u=76281980&t=33)** You might have differences between how you simulate the model and how it's actually being used.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hosting-and-running-your-ai-models?u=76281980&t=37)** The third one is integrations.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hosting-and-running-your-ai-models?u=76281980&t=40)** Depending where your model's being deployed and what systems it needs to connect to, these integrations might be very challenging.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hosting-and-running-your-ai-models?u=76281980&t=46)** The fourth reason is that training data and real world data might be quite different.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hosting-and-running-your-ai-models?u=76281980&t=52)** This could impact the performance of your model.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hosting-and-running-your-ai-models?u=76281980&t=54)** Fifth reason could be latency and throughput challenges.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hosting-and-running-your-ai-models?u=76281980&t=58)** Your model might not perform up to user expectations.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hosting-and-running-your-ai-models?u=76281980&t=61)** And finally, your source data and your model might have sovereignty challenges for compliance or regulatory reasons.
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hosting-and-running-your-ai-models?u=76281980&t=69)** And many of the challenges that you'll experience are similar to software development challenges.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hosting-and-running-your-ai-models?u=76281980&t=73)** If you're working in a siloed way, your development will suffer.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hosting-and-running-your-ai-models?u=76281980&t=76)** So it's important to think about deployment before training.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hosting-and-running-your-ai-models?u=76281980&t=79)** Let's go through an example.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hosting-and-running-your-ai-models?u=76281980&t=81)** If you have a low latency requirement, you might need to take into consideration some things when training.
>
> **[1:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hosting-and-running-your-ai-models?u=76281980&t=87)** For example, you should consider using a smaller model, spend more time on optimization techniques for latency and research the hardware you're deploying on before going through the training process.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hosting-and-running-your-ai-models?u=76281980&t=99)** So in essence, this forms the circular loop.
>
> **[1:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hosting-and-running-your-ai-models?u=76281980&t=102)** Model development and model deployment should be an iterative process with teams communicating and working together.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hosting-and-running-your-ai-models?u=76281980&t=109)** So even though I separated these into separate chapters, they're part of a unified process.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hosting-and-running-your-ai-models?u=76281980&t=114)** Another example is deploying a GDPR compliant model.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hosting-and-running-your-ai-models?u=76281980&t=118)** For GDPR compliant models, we need to make sure that we have explicit consent on the training data.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hosting-and-running-your-ai-models?u=76281980&t=123)** This will affect how we gather data in our user feedback system.
>
> **[2:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hosting-and-running-your-ai-models?u=76281980&t=127)** Oftentimes, we also need to host our data and our model in the EU.
>
> **[2:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hosting-and-running-your-ai-models?u=76281980&t=132)** If we're working in specific sectors like healthcare or finance, there're even stricter requirements.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hosting-and-running-your-ai-models?u=76281980&t=138)** Now, hosting a model is similar to running software.
>
> **[2:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hosting-and-running-your-ai-models?u=76281980&t=140)** It's usually considered to be OpEx, and it'll depend which kind of hardware you use for these operations.
>
> **[2:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hosting-and-running-your-ai-models?u=76281980&t=147)** It really depends on the use case.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hosting-and-running-your-ai-models?u=76281980&t=149)** So in the next video, we'll go through some case studies to look at AI hardware hosting options and dive deeper into the cost analysis.

> **[3:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/choosing-the-right-hardware-for-ai-models?u=76281980&t=204)** Spot instances are when a cloud vendor offers a certain piece of hardware, but can reclaim it at any time.
>
> **[3:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/choosing-the-right-hardware-for-ai-models?u=76281980&t=210)** And because of that, if we're running short batch jobs, it might be a perfect use case to take advantage for cost savings.

> **[4:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/choosing-the-right-hardware-for-ai-models?u=76281980&t=248)** Now, all of these meet our latency requirements, 'cause the average person's reaction time is 200 milliseconds.
>
> **[4:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/choosing-the-right-hardware-for-ai-models?u=76281980&t=253)** Now, chatbots need to be run continuously, so these costs per hour actually add up.
>

>
> **[4:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/choosing-the-right-hardware-for-ai-models?u=76281980&t=264)** And from a deployment perspective, we're going to have three different deployments of the same model, 'cause we want to have high availability.
>
> **[4:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/choosing-the-right-hardware-for-ai-models?u=76281980&t=272)** People rely on our chatbot for continuous access, and we need to make sure that we can deliver.
>
> **[4:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/choosing-the-right-hardware-for-ai-models?u=76281980&t=277)** And from a location perspective, we're going to deploy per region to reduce the latency and comply with any data sovereignty or model sovereignty rules.
>

>
> **[4:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/choosing-the-right-hardware-for-ai-models?u=76281980&t=294)** In the next chapter, we're going to learn about logging and monitoring for AI inference.
>
> **[4:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/choosing-the-right-hardware-for-ai-models?u=76281980&t=298)** If our models have any issues, we want to make sure we know when they happen.
>
> **[5:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/choosing-the-right-hardware-for-ai-models?u=76281980&t=303)** AI downtime is no joke.

> **[6:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/logging-and-monitoring-ai-inference?u=76281980&t=396)** So how do you do logging and monitoring for AI systems?

> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hiring-the-team-for-ai-inference?u=76281980&t=33)** Now getting into the business knowledge, it's also important to understand the usage patterns of these apps and digging into how the users will consume them.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hiring-the-team-for-ai-inference?u=76281980&t=41)** Model optimization is about understanding the business requirements and making the model perform to those standards.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hiring-the-team-for-ai-inference?u=76281980&t=48)** This might include technical things like post-training optimizations with techniques like compiling or quantizing the model.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hiring-the-team-for-ai-inference?u=76281980&t=55)** In certain cases, to get the model to perform at the level that you need, you might need specialty hardware knowledge.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hiring-the-team-for-ai-inference?u=76281980&t=62)** For example, there's a great blog post that Hugging Face put out, to how to optimize the BERT model to get under a one millisecond latency.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hiring-the-team-for-ai-inference?u=76281980&t=70)** This blog post is a technical read, but it is very interesting to understand the thinking and process of optimizing your models.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hiring-the-team-for-ai-inference?u=76281980&t=76)** Now on top of optimizing your models, you need to be able to manage the infrastructure that you run these services on.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hiring-the-team-for-ai-inference?u=76281980&t=82)** This includes choosing the right hardware, being able to scale with demand, and optimize the costs for your budget.
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hiring-the-team-for-ai-inference?u=76281980&t=90)** And you also need to integrate these models with other services so the integration layer becomes very important.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hiring-the-team-for-ai-inference?u=76281980&t=96)** Now going back to the previous video, we talked about how important model observability is, and in this case, we want our team that is managing the deployments to implement logging and monitoring solutions.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hiring-the-team-for-ai-inference?u=76281980&t=108)** They need to be able to set up alerting and when something goes wrong, work with the training team to understand the issues and address them.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hiring-the-team-for-ai-inference?u=76281980&t=115)** Now, as the team scales and becomes larger, people might need to become more specialized to work more efficiently.
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hiring-the-team-for-ai-inference?u=76281980&t=121)** And as you're working with larger models, they'll become harder to deploy compared to more traditional ones.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hiring-the-team-for-ai-inference?u=76281980&t=126)** This is why when running a large language model or other generative AI, people who can deploy these models and put them into production efficiently are paid very well.
>
> **[2:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hiring-the-team-for-ai-inference?u=76281980&t=136)** In the next video, you'll receive a challenge for running AI for your start-up.
>
> **[2:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/hiring-the-team-for-ai-inference?u=76281980&t=140)** This will be a cost estimation exercise in understanding the moving parts we need to succeed.

>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-running-ai-for-your-start-up?u=76281980&t=67)** Now in line 15, we have our scaling strategy.
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-running-ai-for-your-start-up?u=76281980&t=69)** So since we're a startup and we want to keep costs low and we have that 15 minute latency requirement, we can keep just one instance of the CPU running.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-running-ai-for-your-start-up?u=76281980&t=79)** And if we get more throughput, we'll just autoscale.

#### Solution: Running AI for your enterprise
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-running-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-running-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Let's go through our sample solution.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-running-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=8)** Now, since this template is pretty similar to the startup one, I'll only be going through the differences.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-running-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=14)** So starting off, we've updated our Average Requests and our Max Requests on lines 3 and 4.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-running-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=20)** Based on these updates for lines 10 and 11, we can see the amount of hardware units we need are much higher for the maximum number of CPUs that we'll need.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-running-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=29)** We get into the 3000s, which is pretty high.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-running-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=32)** On lines 12 and 13, I've added an extra row for the high-availability configuration.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-running-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=38)** This is only necessary for the A100, since to achieve the throughput we need, we'll automatically go above three units.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-running-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=46)** Now, scrolling down to lines 14 and 15, we can see that our costs are much higher.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-running-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=52)** This makes sense since we're handling a higher throughput.
>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-running-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=56)** Now for a scaling strategy, we're going to maintain the average number of units needed as the minimum.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-running-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=62)** We have a strict latency requirement of one minute, so we want to minimize the amount of scaling that we need to do.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-running-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=67)** Now, if we go to line 19, we'll see our Gross cost per month.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-running-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=72)** And using our ongoing usage discount, we're going to get our model cost per month.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-running-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=76)** In this case, we end up seeing that the T4 is the cheapest option at around $1,800.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-running-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=83)** Now, heading over to the right side of the spreadsheet, for a Team structure on line J2, we've chosen a team of size 4, the same as our training team in a previous exercise.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-running-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=94)** Our hourly rate is 250,000, and our project length is 3 months.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-running-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=99)** We've assigned the same fractional maintenance of 25% of the team size to maintain and debug the model.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-running-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=106)** Now, heading over to columns F and G, we can see here that our additional tooling is more expensive.
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-running-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=112)** This is because we're an enterprise, but are also handling a much larger scale.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-running-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=117)** So we've estimated that our Logging chargeback is going to be $2,000 a month.
>
> **[2:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-running-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=122)** Our Monitoring chargeback is going to be 5,000.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-running-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=125)** And our Data tools for streaming the data is going to be a 100,000.
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-running-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=129)** And notice here that this isn't a cost, but a chargeback.
>
> **[2:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-running-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=132)** We'll assume that another team will be paying for this and they'll be charging us back for our average costs.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-running-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=138)** As scrolling down, we can see our Tooling Costs for a month, it's going to be 107,000.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-running-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=144)** Our initial development costs will be 250,000 by having four engineers work for three months.
>
> **[2:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-running-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=150)** On line G16, our Ongoing Labor cost is our fractional maintenance times our team size times our monthly rate.
>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-running-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=159)** Now heading over to G18, we can see that this is our T4 cost, our cheapest model option.
>
> **[2:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-running-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=165)** Now in G20, our Total Monthly Cost comes up to $129,647.73, and for the year.
>
> **[2:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-running-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=174)** Adding our initial development cost and our total cost is going to be around $1.8 million.
>
> **[3:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-running-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=180)** For our budget ask, we're going to ask for $2 million to deploy and maintain this project.
>
> **[3:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-running-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=186)** And there we go.
>
> **[3:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-running-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=187)** We've estimated a sample solution for deploying a model in an enterprise environment.
>
> **[3:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/solution-running-ai-for-your-enterprise?u=76281980&t=191)** In the next chapter, we're going to talk about the costs of running these models beyond just financial costs.

### 6. Other Costs

#### AI copyright and legal risks
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-copyright-and-legal-risks?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-copyright-and-legal-risks?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] In this chapter, we'll talk about the other costs of AI that are beyond financial.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-copyright-and-legal-risks?u=76281980&t=5)** In this video, we'll talk about some of the copyright and legal risks of AI.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-copyright-and-legal-risks?u=76281980&t=10)** So an important question to ask is, where does the data used for training AI models come from?
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-copyright-and-legal-risks?u=76281980&t=16)** In the case of GenAI, it's lots of internet data.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-copyright-and-legal-risks?u=76281980&t=21)** But much of this data is still covered by copyright.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-copyright-and-legal-risks?u=76281980&t=24)** In December 2023, "The New York Times" filed a lawsuit against OpenAI and Microsoft about allegations of copyright infringement.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-copyright-and-legal-risks?u=76281980&t=33)** The main argument is that ChatGPT could produce "New York Times" content verbatim, content that was behind a paywall.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-copyright-and-legal-risks?u=76281980&t=39)** For the training of these models, OpenAI argues fair use.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-copyright-and-legal-risks?u=76281980&t=44)** This lawsuit is very important since it'll likely set the precedent for many AI lawsuits in the future.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-copyright-and-legal-risks?u=76281980&t=50)** Another example is that, in November 2022, four plaintiffs argued that Microsoft Copilot was generating AI suggestions that infringed on code copyright.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-copyright-and-legal-risks?u=76281980&t=60)** Now, lawsuits can be scary for companies, and because of this, many potential customers of GenAI could be scared off.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-copyright-and-legal-risks?u=76281980&t=67)** For this reason, Google and Microsoft have pledged to cover legal costs for GenAI copyright.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-copyright-and-legal-risks?u=76281980&t=73)** This was announced in September 2023 for Microsoft, and October 2023 for Google.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-copyright-and-legal-risks?u=76281980&t=78)** There's also a legal risk for model bias.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-copyright-and-legal-risks?u=76281980&t=81)** In September 2023, there's a ruling on model bias where tutoring company iTutorGroup was told to pay $365,000 to settle a discrimination case.
>
> **[1:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-copyright-and-legal-risks?u=76281980&t=93)** The model was deemed to be biased, discriminating on people over the age of 55.
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-copyright-and-legal-risks?u=76281980&t=98)** Now, the third risk is the legal risk for model output.
>
> **[1:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-copyright-and-legal-risks?u=76281980&t=102)** In February of 2024, it was ruled that Air Canada needed to refund a customer based on a policy that a chatbot had given.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-copyright-and-legal-risks?u=76281980&t=110)** Court ruling indicated that the airline was responsible for its chatbot output.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-copyright-and-legal-risks?u=76281980&t=114)** So if a chatbot miscommunicates some information, the companies might be liable to what information was said.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-copyright-and-legal-risks?u=76281980&t=120)** In this case, it was a free ticket.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-copyright-and-legal-risks?u=76281980&t=123)** The three legal risks highlighted the legal risk for copyright, model bias and model output should all be reviewed by our lawyers.
>
> **[2:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-copyright-and-legal-risks?u=76281980&t=132)** And in the next video, we'll talk about the nebulous concept of AI reputational risk.

#### AI reputational risks
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-reputational-risks?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-reputational-risks?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Narrator] In this video, we'll discuss the potential reputational risks of AI.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-reputational-risks?u=76281980&t=5)** Many large companies are conservative risk-wise in order to see how customers first perceive a solution and to mitigate the risk to their reputation.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-reputational-risks?u=76281980&t=13)** Now, in the current AI wave, risk appetite about AI has increased significantly with almost 10x the amount of AI mentions in earning calls in 2023 on S&P 500 transcripts.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-reputational-risks?u=76281980&t=26)** And many companies who don't have expertise in AI may launch products prematurely and mishandled this opportunity.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-reputational-risks?u=76281980&t=33)** For example, recently a car dealership when viral after their bot was a simple wrapper on ChatGPT and customers we're able to say to give them a car for just $1.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-reputational-risks?u=76281980&t=43)** Now, on top of these mishaps, reputational risk can also occur when there's an underwhelming launch.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-reputational-risks?u=76281980&t=49)** When a company says, "This feature is powered by AI," sometimes it's just an outsourced manual labor job or a quick demo thrown together.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-reputational-risks?u=76281980&t=57)** Conversely, a well implemented use case with a smooth customer experience may enhance the reputation of a company as being innovative and customer friendly.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-reputational-risks?u=76281980&t=66)** So as a company, it's important to know your customer profile and expectations and balance the time to market testing and feature implementation of your AI products.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-reputational-risks?u=76281980&t=76)** In the next video, we'll talk about AI security risks and how they might impact your company.

#### AI security risks
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] As we deploy more AI models, AI security risks become more important.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=6)** In this video, we'll cover some of the types of AI security vulnerabilities, ways to mitigate, and the impacts that these might have on your business.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=16)** Now there are a few ways to compromise your AI system.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=18)** First is finding exploits in the data input that goes into the model.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=23)** The second one is poisoning the training data.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=26)** The third one is prompt injection, and the fourth one is data extraction.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=32)** And for many AI systems, it's possible to find certain input patterns that lead to unexpected results.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=39)** In this example, we see that a panda with some random image noise might be classified as a gibbon, even though the image itself doesn't change, and there's been lots of research in this area.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=50)** There are potential business impacts.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=52)** One might be, if your system uses something like automated receipt scanning, is it possible for this automated system to be compromised?
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=60)** The second example of a potential impact is with self-driving cars.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=64)** What happens if you show a self-driving car a green light rather than a red light, or the angle of the sun confuses the vehicle?
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=71)** There are pretty large societal impacts.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=74)** Now thankfully, there's been lots of research to make models more robust to these types of attacks.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=79)** However, if you have access to the training data, it's possible to compromise these models more easily.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=85)** One example is the nightshade attack.
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=88)** With a combination of different training data and prompts, it is possible for generative models to generate the wrong type of image, for example, generating a handbag into a toaster.
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=100)** So before launching your models, it's important to do something called red teaming, which is doing internal adversarial testing to figure out what might go wrong.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=109)** On the other side of the spectrum, there's something called blue teaming, which is the exercise of doing internal defense, and the AI security space is pretty new.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=118)** So there are a few initiatives launching that might be helpful.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=120)** For example, for LLMs, Meta launched the Purple LLaMa Initiative providing some tools for teams to both red team and blue team these types of large language models.
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=131)** And moving on to the large language model side, for large language model apps, there are two main dangers.
>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=137)** They might, one, leak info that they're not supposed to, and two, they might do the wrong type of task.
>
> **[2:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=143)** Now many of these large language model apps, such as RAG-based ones, provide automated access to documentation.
>
> **[2:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=150)** Now the tricky part might be is providing access to the right documentation.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=155)** For example, when Amazon launched their Q chatbot, there are issues within the first couple of days of being able to use prompts to surface information that was classified as confidential.
>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=166)** This resulted in a pretty fast response from Amazon, but even a large company can make mistakes in these types of product launches.
>
> **[2:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=173)** Now this type of compromise was able to be surfaced by fairly intermediate developers.
>
> **[2:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=179)** Now there are even more advanced techniques that can get through even the most stringent security teams.
>
> **[3:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=184)** For example, in 2023, there's a more complex technique used on Google Bard.
>
> **[3:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=189)** The idea of the compromise was, by using markdown images, you're able to expose some of the information in people's Google Docs.
>
> **[3:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=197)** Now the good thing is that these large LLM providers and companies usually do a great job of patching up these vulnerabilities quickly.
>
> **[3:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=204)** But as a team building this technology yourself, you need to be extra careful.
>
> **[3:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=209)** It's important to have the correct guardrails in place to mitigate these kinds of harms.
>
> **[3:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=213)** So there are a few ways of doing this.
>
> **[3:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=215)** The first one is verifying the data, both the training data and the data coming in as input.
>
> **[3:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=221)** You want to make sure that you understand where your data's coming from and how it's being used.
>
> **[3:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=226)** The second technique is using a security technique called least privilege.
>
> **[3:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=230)** Least privilege means only grant a person or an application the minimum amount of permissions that you need to be successful.
>
> **[3:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=237)** So what this means is don't grant an application access to all your data if you don't need to.
>
> **[4:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=242)** This reduces the attack surface that potential adversaries can use to gain access to your information.
>
> **[4:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=248)** The next item is just do lots of testing.
>
> **[4:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=251)** Whether it's formal red teaming or just understanding your data and your scenarios, testing these applications is extremely important.
>
> **[4:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=259)** And finally, it's important to adopt standard software best practices.
>
> **[4:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=262)** While we've only covered the techniques that can be used against AI models, standard security vulnerabilities through software or social engineering can also be very effective.
>
> **[4:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=273)** Now finally, let's talk about some of the business impacts involved.
>
> **[4:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=276)** Many of these attackers are after private data access, meaning personal information or confidential information.
>
> **[4:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=282)** So your business might be impacted if this information is accessed.
>
> **[4:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=286)** The other risk is potential automated fraud.
>
> **[4:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=289)** As I mentioned earlier, if you have automated systems that do some kind of financial processing, you want to make sure that the numbers that are being passed through are verified, not just through AI.
>
> **[5:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=301)** Also, there might be a legal risk.
>
> **[5:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=302)** If shareholders or other stakeholders feel that you're not providing an adequate amount of defense for adversarial attacks on your systems, you may be sued, or other litigatory action may be taken.
>
> **[5:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=313)** Now AI security is a complex issue.
>
> **[5:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=316)** I recommend diving deeper into this with security experts when reviewing your applications.
>
> **[5:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-security-risks?u=76281980&t=321)** In the next video, we'll talk more about service-level agreements and the risks and costs when using AI.

#### AI's environmental impacts
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-s-environmental-impacts?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-s-environmental-impacts?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Presenter] In this video, we'll talk about the environmental costs of AI.
>
> **[0:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-s-environmental-impacts?u=76281980&t=3)** So AI uses many resources along the many steps along the way.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-s-environmental-impacts?u=76281980&t=8)** This includes data collection and processing, training, and inference.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-s-environmental-impacts?u=76281980&t=13)** Let's talk about the resources that we use.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-s-environmental-impacts?u=76281980&t=15)** There are three main resources: Water, electricity, and materials.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-s-environmental-impacts?u=76281980&t=21)** These can be found across the data centers, grid, and chips that are actually used for AI training and inference.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-s-environmental-impacts?u=76281980&t=29)** Starting off with water, researchers from UC Riverside and UT Arlington estimate that global AI demand may result in 4.2 to 6.6 billion cubic meters of water usage by 2027.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-s-environmental-impacts?u=76281980&t=41)** That's roughly half the water consumption of the UK.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-s-environmental-impacts?u=76281980&t=45)** And this water consumption largely goes to data center cooling where these models are being trained and run.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-s-environmental-impacts?u=76281980&t=50)** And for training an individual model like GPT 3, the researchers estimate that it used around 5.4 million liters of water.
>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-s-environmental-impacts?u=76281980&t=56)** And for running something like ChatGPT, 5 or 10 prompts might use around two cups of water.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-s-environmental-impacts?u=76281980&t=61)** Now, most cloud vendors have pledged to be water positive by 2030.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-s-environmental-impacts?u=76281980&t=65)** This is especially important in the next few years as we face more extreme weather and drought.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-s-environmental-impacts?u=76281980&t=70)** And from the electricity side, according to researchers from University of Washington, it's estimated to have used around 10 gigawatt hours of power to train one instance of ChatGPT.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-s-environmental-impacts?u=76281980&t=80)** That's around as much power as a thousand houses used per year.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-s-environmental-impacts?u=76281980&t=84)** Now for running ChatGPT once it's trained, it's estimated that it uses around one gigawatt hour a day, or the equivalent of 33,000 houses.
>
> **[1:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-s-environmental-impacts?u=76281980&t=93)** Now, beyond just the amount of electricity that's used, it's important to consider the electricity carbon intensity.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-s-environmental-impacts?u=76281980&t=99)** This means how much carbon is emitted per electricity used.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-s-environmental-impacts?u=76281980&t=103)** So looking at four different regions, ranging from Montreal, Toronto, Paris, and Los Angeles, we can see that the carbon intensity is quite different.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-s-environmental-impacts?u=76281980&t=113)** One of the columns shows us how much renewable power is actually being used, with Montreal using renewable power almost a hundred percent of the time.
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-s-environmental-impacts?u=76281980&t=121)** The right column shows us how intensive the local carbon grid is.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-s-environmental-impacts?u=76281980&t=125)** The higher this value, the more carbon emissions we produce per amount of power.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-s-environmental-impacts?u=76281980&t=130)** So the recommendation here is to try to choose a region with lower carbon intensity.
>
> **[2:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-s-environmental-impacts?u=76281980&t=135)** Now, in training models, it's becoming more common to disclose the carbon impact.
>
> **[2:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-s-environmental-impacts?u=76281980&t=139)** One recent example is from LLaMa 2 where they disclose how much GPU hours they used, the power consumption of each, and the total carbon emitted.
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-s-environmental-impacts?u=76281980&t=148)** And one thing that this misses is the electricity power from the other chips that are being used that we talked about, the compute, RAM, disk, and cooling systems, along with the power and materials needed to build the data centers that power all these chips.
>
> **[2:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-s-environmental-impacts?u=76281980&t=163)** So often, when we estimate the environmental impact of AI models, we forget the manufacturing impact.
>
> **[2:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-s-environmental-impacts?u=76281980&t=169)** Since we have to build the chips, data centers, and all the surrounding infrastructure around them.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-s-environmental-impacts?u=76281980&t=175)** Now, speaking about the chips, AI chip demand has been increasing exponentially in the last few years.
>
> **[3:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-s-environmental-impacts?u=76281980&t=181)** With this skyrocketing demand, all these chips require materials like rare earths to be built.
>
> **[3:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-s-environmental-impacts?u=76281980&t=187)** This requires significant mining intensity to find, extract, and develop these materials.
>
> **[3:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-s-environmental-impacts?u=76281980&t=193)** So overall, AI has significant environmental impacts.
>
> **[3:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-s-environmental-impacts?u=76281980&t=197)** So what can you do about it?
>
> **[3:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-s-environmental-impacts?u=76281980&t=199)** Well, the first step is to educate the team and make sure that they understand what the impacts are.
>
> **[3:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-s-environmental-impacts?u=76281980&t=204)** The next step is to disclose your impact and run the estimates to understand what your impact is.
>
> **[3:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-s-environmental-impacts?u=76281980&t=209)** You can reduce this impact by choosing cloud regions that have low carbon and water intensity.
>
> **[3:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-s-environmental-impacts?u=76281980&t=214)** And finally, you can run smaller models when possible in order to reduce the environmental impact of your work.
>
> **[3:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-s-environmental-impacts?u=76281980&t=221)** So this wraps up this chapter on AI risks and other costs.
>
> **[3:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/ai-s-environmental-impacts?u=76281980&t=225)** In the next chapter, we'll be talking about generating revenue with AI models.

### 7. Revenue-Generating Models

#### Unit and margin pricing for AI
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/unit-and-margin-pricing-for-ai?u=76281980)

>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/unit-and-margin-pricing-for-ai?u=76281980&t=5)** So far, our chapters have been about the cost of AI.

>

>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/unit-and-margin-pricing-for-ai?u=76281980&t=69)** Let's assume our customers are using this product over time.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/unit-and-margin-pricing-for-ai?u=76281980&t=73)** Every day, different users use the product in different volumes.
>
> **[1:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/unit-and-margin-pricing-for-ai?u=76281980&t=77)** As you can see here, our costs, requests, and revenue are all moving together.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/unit-and-margin-pricing-for-ai?u=76281980&t=83)** With this technique, our margin is fixed at 50%.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/unit-and-margin-pricing-for-ai?u=76281980&t=86)** If our requests double, so will our costs and our revenue.
>

>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/unit-and-margin-pricing-for-ai?u=76281980&t=99)** Now, some of our models might be run in a different way.
>
> **[1:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/ai-pricing-and-roi-a-technical-breakdown/unit-and-margin-pricing-for-ai?u=76281980&t=102)** They might be run continuously.
>

>

>

>
